"Huh, perhaps if I continue to live, I will die?" I think that every human has been confronted with this question, but as a relatively young book author, I had bumped into this question, "Absurd absurd, there's no way people die!", and with that stupid conclusion I had closed the question. And, it's natural, but humans can die. One day they will die for sure. It feels like 'what are you saying' but it seems it's already decided. It's not even decent. It's not a joke. Even if the person in charge came out, that person in charge will eventually die. No matter how much you stretch out your life expectancy or how much you lower the probability of death, day by day, living through a day in itself is like augmenting the probability of death apparently. So, if there was a box where inside there were winning lottery tickets, and the ratio between winning and losing was about forty thousand to one, so that even if you drew one per day you would still end up losing. Even then, the fact that, day by day, people are living with unreliable and unfounded ways to win like "the tickets on that side seem to be winning ones" or "the ones on the top aren't mixed so they are dangerous", and mere consolations like "normally you don't draw that kind of thing" is something sad. When you die you will die even if you get hit by a meteorite. Lottery is a gamble, but if the probabilities to earn are low enough then it's no longer gambling, or something like that.

Further talk would just be sloppy and have no correlation with the characters appearing in this book, but the key person of the book, Madoka Kuchiha, is an immortal girl. Even if it's a first person narrator, since it's also written elsewhere, it's ninety nine percent certainly true. But if the parts under the words of established 'life and death' aren't steady, then I'm worried even though it's other people's a airs. Well, if you were to say that the Niounomiya siblings are just an entity that divides in two parts the strength and weakness that was originally one, to begin with they are just bridges that failed to lead the narrator that is the nonsense using protagonist to death and they aren't even living properly, it seems like only characters whose problem aren't things like living or dying are appearing, it's not like the book is not wobbling, really I don't know what karma led to things ending up like this, but like that the last boss appeared, it was

"Cannibal Magical : The Niounomiya siblings of magical massacre".

Now, as for editor in-charge Ooda Katsushi-sama and illustrator in-charge Take-san, I would like to do the usual acknowledgments, but I'm beginning to run out of variations of how to thank them. I no longer know what to say, but even if I run out of words to thank them with , my feeling of gratitude won't run out.
